<div id="impact-of-natural-disasters-on-the-economy-and-the-public-health-of-the-united-states" class="section level1">
<h1>Impact Of Natural Disasters On The Economy And The Public Health Of The United States</h1>
<p>Storms and other severe weather events can cause both public health and economic problems for communities and municipalities. Many severe events can result in fatalities, injuries, and property damage, and preventing such outcomes to the extent possible is a key concern.<br />This project involves exploring the U.S. National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administrationâs (NOAA) storm database. This database tracks characteristics of major storms and weather events in the United States, including when and where they occur, as well as estimates of any fatalities, injuries, and property damage.</p>
<div id="synopsis" class="section level2">
<h2>Synopsis</h2>
<p>This report consists in analyzing the NOAA storm database containing data on extreme climate events. This data was collected during the period from 1950 through 2011. The purpose of this analysis is to answer the following two questions:<br />1. Across the United States, which types of events (as indicated in the EVTYPE variable) are most harmful with respect to population health?<br />2. Across the United States, which types of events have the greatest economic consequences?</p>
<p>I used the weather events specified in the documentation (paragraphs 7.1 - 7.48).<br />Main conclusions of the study:<br />1. Tornado is the most hazordous climate event with more than 5600 deaths and 91400 injuries.<br />2. Floods have caused the most significant economic damage - more than 157 billion USD.</p>

<div id="data-processing" class="section level2">
<h2>Data Processing</h2>
<p>The analysis was performed on <a href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/stormevents/ftp.jsp">Storm Events Database</a>, provided by <a href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/">National Climatic Data Center</a>. The data is from a comma-separated-value file available <a href="https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2FStormData.csv.bz2">here</a>.<br />There is also some documentation of the data available <a href="https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fpeer2_doc%2Fpd01016005curr.pdf">here</a>.</p>
<p>First, we download the data file and unzip it.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>setwd(&quot;C:/Users/Utkarsh/Documents/GitHub/Reproducible-Research-Johns-Hopkins-Bloomberg-School-of-Public-Health-Coursera/Project 02/&quot;)
if (!&quot;StormData.csv.bz2&quot; %in% dir(&quot;./&quot;)) {
print(&quot;Downloading File.....&quot;)
download.file(&quot;http://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2FStormData.csv.bz2&quot;, destfile = &quot;StormData.csv.bz2&quot;)
}</code></pre>
<p>Then, we read the generated csv file. If the data already exists in the working environment, we do not need to load it again. Otherwise, we read the csv file.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>if (!&quot;storm&quot; %in% ls()) {
storm &lt;- read.csv(bzfile(&quot;StormData.csv.bz2&quot;), sep = &quot;,&quot;, header = TRUE, stringsAsFactors = FALSE)
}
dim(storm)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 902297 37</code></pre>
<p>Extract data corresponding to the 48 events as described in the documentation paragraphs 7.1 through 7.48</p>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Vector of 48 events as defined in the documentation:</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>events &lt;- c(&quot;Astronomical Low Tide&quot;, &quot;Avalanche&quot;, &quot;Blizzard&quot;, &quot;Coastal Flood&quot;, &quot;Cold/Wind Chill&quot;, &quot;Debris Flow&quot;, &quot;Dense Fog&quot;, &quot;Dense Smoke&quot;, &quot;Drought&quot;, &quot;Dust Devil&quot;, &quot;Dust Storm&quot;, &quot;Excessive Heat&quot;, &quot;Extreme cold/Wind Chill&quot;, &quot;Flash Flood&quot;, &quot;Flood&quot;, &quot;Freezing&quot;, &quot;Frost/Freeze&quot;, &quot;Funnel Cloud&quot;, &quot;Hail&quot;, &quot;Heat&quot;, &quot;Heavy Rain&quot;, &quot;Heavy Snow&quot;, &quot;High Surf&quot;, &quot;High Wind&quot;, &quot;Hurricane/Typhoon&quot;, &quot;Ice Storm&quot;, &quot;Lakeshore Flood&quot;, &quot;Lake-Effect Snow&quot;, &quot;Lightning&quot;, &quot;Marine Hail&quot;, &quot;Marine High Wind&quot;, &quot;Marine Strong Wind&quot;, &quot;Marine Thunderstorm Wind&quot;, &quot;Rip Current&quot;, &quot;Seiche&quot;, &quot;Sleet&quot;, &quot;Storm Tide&quot;, &quot;Strong Wind&quot;, &quot;Thunderstorm Wind&quot;, &quot;Tornado&quot;, &quot;Tropical Depression&quot;, &quot;Tropical Storm&quot;, &quot;Tsunami&quot;, &quot;Volcanic Ash&quot;, &quot;Waterspout&quot;, &quot;Wildfire&quot;, &quot;Winter Storm&quot;, &quot;Winter Weather&quot;) </code></pre>
<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Some events are combined events separated with a slash (e.g âHurricane/Typhoonâ). I will use regular expressions to extract either a combined event (Hurricane/Typhoon) or any part of it (Hurricane or Typhoon)</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>events_regex &lt;- c(&quot;Astronomical Low Tide|Low Tide&quot;, &quot;Avalanche&quot;, &quot;Blizzard&quot;, &quot;Coastal Flood&quot;, &quot;Cold/Wind Chill&quot;, &quot;Debris Flow&quot;, &quot;Dense Fog&quot;, &quot;Dense Smoke&quot;, &quot;Drought&quot;, &quot;Dust Devil&quot;, &quot;Dust Storm&quot;, &quot;Excessive Heat&quot;, &quot;Extreme cold/Wind Chill|Extreme Cold|Wind Chill&quot;, &quot;Flash Flood&quot;, &quot;Flood&quot;, &quot;Freezing&quot;, &quot;Frost/Freeze|Frost|Freeze&quot;, &quot;Funnel Cloud&quot;, &quot;Hail&quot;, &quot;Heat&quot;, &quot;Heavy Rain&quot;, &quot;Heavy Snow&quot;, &quot;High Surf&quot;, &quot;High Wind&quot;, &quot;Hurricane/Typhoon|Hurricane|Typhoon&quot;, &quot;Ice Storm&quot;, &quot;Lakeshore Flood&quot;, &quot;Lake-Effect Snow&quot;, &quot;Lightning&quot;, &quot;Marine Hail&quot;, &quot;Marine High Wind&quot;, &quot;Marine Strong Wind&quot;, &quot;Marine Thunderstorm Wind|Marine tstm Wind&quot;, &quot;Rip Current&quot;, &quot;Seiche&quot;, &quot;Sleet&quot;, &quot;Storm Tide&quot;, &quot;Strong Wind&quot;, &quot;Thunderstorm Wind|tstm wind&quot;, &quot;Tornado&quot;, &quot;Tropical Depression&quot;, &quot;Tropical Storm&quot;, &quot;Tsunami&quot;, &quot;Volcanic Ash&quot;, &quot;Waterspout&quot;, &quot;Wildfire&quot;, &quot;Winter Storm&quot;, &quot;Winter Weather&quot;) </code></pre>
<ol start="3" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>The next step is to extract rows corresponding to the event from the documentation, I will also choose the columns which are relevant to our analysis:<br /></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>EVTYPE -&gt; Type of event<br /></li>
<li>FATALITIES -&gt; Number of fatalities<br /></li>
<li>INJURIES -&gt; Number of injuries<br /></li>
<li>PROPDMG -&gt; Amount of property damage in orders of magnitude<br /></li>
<li>PROPDMGEXP -&gt; Order of magnitude for property damage (e.g.Â K for thousands)<br /></li>
<li>CROPDMG -&gt; Amount of crop damage in orders of magnitude<br /></li>
<li>PROPDMGEXP -&gt; Order of magnitude for crop damage (e.g.Â M for millions)</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>options(scipen = 999) # force fixed notation of numbers instead of scientific
cleandata &lt;- data.frame(EVTYPE = character(0), FATALITIES = numeric(0), INJURIES = numeric(0), PROPDMG = numeric(0), PROPDMGEXP = character(0), CROPDMG = numeric(0), CROPDMGEXP = character(0))
for (i in 1:length(events)) {
rows &lt;- storm[grep(events_regex[i], ignore.case = TRUE, storm$EVTYPE), ]
rows &lt;- rows[, c(&quot;EVTYPE&quot;, &quot;FATALITIES&quot;, &quot;INJURIES&quot;, &quot;PROPDMG&quot;, &quot;PROPDMGEXP&quot;, &quot;CROPDMG&quot;, &quot;CROPDMGEXP&quot;)]
CLEANNAME &lt;- c(rep(events[i], nrow(rows)))
rows &lt;- cbind(rows, CLEANNAME)
cleandata &lt;- rbind(cleandata, rows)
}</code></pre>
<ol start="4" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Take into account the order of magnitude of property and crop damage (H = hundreds, K = thousands, M = millions, B= billions)</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code># convert letter exponents to integers
cleandata[(cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;K&quot; | cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;k&quot;), ]$PROPDMGEXP &lt;- 3
cleandata[(cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;M&quot; | cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;m&quot;), ]$PROPDMGEXP &lt;- 6
cleandata[(cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;B&quot; | cleandata$PROPDMGEXP == &quot;b&quot;), ]$PROPDMGEXP &lt;- 9
cleandata[(cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;K&quot; | cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;k&quot;), ]$CROPDMGEXP &lt;- 3
cleandata[(cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;M&quot; | cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;m&quot;), ]$CROPDMGEXP &lt;- 6
cleandata[(cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;B&quot; | cleandata$CROPDMGEXP == &quot;b&quot;), ]$CROPDMGEXP &lt;- 9</code></pre>
<ol start="5" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Compute combined economic damage (property damage + crops damage)</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code># multiply property and crops damage by 10 raised to the power of the exponent
suppressWarnings(cleandata$PROPDMG &lt;- cleandata$PROPDMG * 10^as.numeric(cleandata$PROPDMGEXP))
suppressWarnings(cleandata$CROPDMG &lt;- cleandata$CROPDMG * 10^as.numeric(cleandata$CROPDMGEXP))
# compute combined economic damage (property damage + crops damage)
suppressWarnings(TOTECODMG &lt;- cleandata$PROPDMG + cleandata$CROPDMG)
cleandata &lt;- cbind(cleandata, TOTECODMG)
# delete 'PROPDMGEXP' and 'CROPDMGEXP'columns which have become unnecessary after conversion
cleandata &lt;- cleandata[, c(&quot;EVTYPE&quot;, &quot;FATALITIES&quot;, &quot;INJURIES&quot;, &quot;PROPDMG&quot;, &quot;CROPDMG&quot;, &quot;CLEANNAME&quot;, &quot;TOTECODMG&quot;)]</code></pre>
<p>At this stage clean data is ready for plotting graphs.</p>
</div>
<div id="results" class="section level2">
<h2>Results</h2>
<div id="question-01-across-the-united-states-which-types-of-events-are-most-harmful-with-respect-to-population-health" class="section level3">
<h3>Question 01 : Across the United States, which types of events are most harmful with respect to population health?</h3>
<div id="fatalities-and-injuries" class="section level5">
<h5>Fatalities and Injuries</h5>
<p>As for the impact on public health, we have got two sorted lists of severe weather events below by the number of people badly affected.</p>
<ul>
<li>Aggregate Data for Fatalities</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>fatalities &lt;- aggregate(FATALITIES ~ CLEANNAME, data = cleandata, FUN = sum)
fatalities &lt;- fatalities[order(fatalities$FATALITIES, decreasing = TRUE), ]
# 10 most harmful causes of fatalities
MaxFatalities &lt;- fatalities[1:10, ]
print(MaxFatalities) </code></pre>
<pre><code>## CLEANNAME FATALITIES
## 38 Tornado 5661
## 19 Heat 3138
## 11 Excessive Heat 1922
## 14 Flood 1525
## 13 Flash Flood 1035
## 28 Lightning 817
## 37 Thunderstorm Wind 753
## 33 Rip Current 577
## 12 Extreme cold/Wind Chill 382
## 23 High Wind 299</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>Aggregate Data for Injuries</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>injuries &lt;- aggregate(INJURIES ~ CLEANNAME, data = cleandata, FUN = sum)
injuries &lt;- injuries[order(injuries$INJURIES, decreasing = TRUE), ]
# 10 most harmful causes of injuries
MaxInjuries &lt;- injuries[1:10, ]
print(MaxInjuries)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## CLEANNAME INJURIES
## 38 Tornado 91407
## 37 Thunderstorm Wind 9493
## 19 Heat 9224
## 14 Flood 8604
## 11 Excessive Heat 6525
## 28 Lightning 5232
## 25 Ice Storm 1992
## 13 Flash Flood 1802
## 23 High Wind 1523
## 18 Hail 1467</code></pre>
<p>And the following is a pair of graphs of Total Fatalities and Total Injuries caused by these Severe Weather Events.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>par(mfrow = c(1, 2), mar = c(15, 4, 3, 2), mgp = c(3, 1, 0), cex = 0.8)
barplot(MaxFatalities$FATALITIES, las = 3, names.arg = MaxFatalities$CLEANNAME, main = &quot;Weather Events With\n The Top 10 Highest Fatalities&quot;, ylab = &quot;Number of Fatalities&quot;, col = &quot;grey&quot;)
barplot(MaxInjuries$INJURIES, las = 3, names.arg = MaxInjuries$CLEANNAME, main = &quot;Weather Events With\n The Top 10 Highest Injuries&quot;, ylab = &quot;Number of Injuries&quot;, col = &quot;grey&quot;)</code></pre>

title alt width="672" /></p>
<p>Based on the above histograms, we find that <strong>Tornado</strong> and <strong>Heat</strong> had caused most fatalities and <strong>Tornado</strong> had caused most injuries in the United States from 1995 to 2011.</p>
<p>Note: I decided not to compute the total damage consisting of fatalities and injuries (fatalities + injuries) since they have a different order of magnitude (a damage related to 1 death is far greater than a damage related to a light injury, for example). Throughout this report, I have always presented the data relating to fatalities and injuries separately.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="question-02-across-the-united-states-which-types-of-events-have-the-greatest-economic-consequences" class="section level3">
<h3>Question 02 : Across the United States, which types of events have the greatest economic consequences?</h3>
<div id="property-and-crops-combined-economic-damage" class="section level5">
<h5>Property and Crops combined Economic Damage</h5>
<p>As for the impact on economy, we have got two sorted lists below by the amount of money cost by damages.</p>
<ul>
<li>Aggregate Data for Property Damage.</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>propdmg &lt;- aggregate(PROPDMG ~ CLEANNAME, data = cleandata, FUN = sum)
propdmg &lt;- propdmg[order(propdmg$PROPDMG, decreasing = TRUE), ]
# 5 most harmful causes of injuries
propdmgMax &lt;- propdmg[1:10, ]
print(propdmgMax)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## CLEANNAME PROPDMG
## 14 Flood 168212215589
## 24 Hurricane/Typhoon 85356410010
## 38 Tornado 58603317864
## 18 Hail 17622990956
## 13 Flash Flood 17588791879
## 37 Thunderstorm Wind 11575228673
## 40 Tropical Storm 7714390550
## 45 Winter Storm 6749997251
## 23 High Wind 6166300000
## 44 Wildfire 4865614000</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>Aggregate Data for Crop Damage</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>cropdmg &lt;- aggregate(CROPDMG ~ CLEANNAME, data = cleandata, FUN = sum)
cropdmg &lt;- cropdmg[order(cropdmg$CROPDMG, decreasing = TRUE), ]
# 5 most harmful causes of injuries
cropdmgMax &lt;- cropdmg[1:10, ]
print(cropdmgMax)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## CLEANNAME CROPDMG
## 8 Drought 13972621780
## 14 Flood 12380109100
## 24 Hurricane/Typhoon 5516117800
## 25 Ice Storm 5022113500
## 18 Hail 3114212870
## 16 Frost/Freeze 1997061000
## 13 Flash Flood 1532197150
## 12 Extreme cold/Wind Chill 1313623000
## 37 Thunderstorm Wind 1255947980
## 19 Heat 904469280</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>Aggregate Total Economic Damage</li>
</ul>
<pre class="r"><code>ecodmg &lt;- aggregate(TOTECODMG ~ CLEANNAME, data = cleandata, FUN = sum)
ecodmg &lt;- ecodmg[order(ecodmg$TOTECODMG, decreasing = TRUE), ]
# 5 most harmful causes of property damage
ecodmgMax &lt;- ecodmg[1:10, ]
print(ecodmgMax)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## CLEANNAME TOTECODMG
## 14 Flood 157764680787
## 24 Hurricane/Typhoon 44330000800
## 38 Tornado 18172843863
## 18 Hail 11681050140
## 13 Flash Flood 9224527227
## 37 Thunderstorm Wind 7098296330
## 25 Ice Storm 5925150850
## 44 Wildfire 3685468370
## 23 High Wind 3472442200
## 8 Drought 1886667000</code></pre>
<p>And the following are graphs of Total Property Damages, Total Crop Damages and Total Economic Damages caused by these Severe Weather Events.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>par(mfrow = c(1, 3), mar = c(15, 4, 3, 2), mgp = c(3, 1, 0), cex = 0.8)
barplot(propdmgMax$PROPDMG/(10^9), las = 3, names.arg = propdmgMax$CLEANNAME, main = &quot;Top 10 Events with\n Greatest Property Damages&quot;, ylab = &quot;Cost of damages ($ billions)&quot;, col = &quot;grey&quot;)
barplot(cropdmgMax$CROPDMG/(10^9), las = 3, names.arg = cropdmgMax$CLEANNAME, main = &quot;Top 10 Events With\n Greatest Crop Damages&quot;, ylab = &quot;Cost of damages ($ billions)&quot;, col = &quot;grey&quot;)
barplot(ecodmgMax$TOTECODMG/(10^9), las = 3, names.arg = ecodmgMax$CLEANNAME, main = &quot;Top 10 Events With\n Greatest Economic Damages&quot;, ylab = &quot;Cost of damages ($ billions)&quot;, col = &quot;grey&quot;)</code></pre>

<p>The weather events have the Greatest Economic Consequences are: <strong>Flood</strong>, <strong>Drought</strong>, <strong>Tornado</strong> and <strong>Typhoon</strong>.<br />Across the United States, <strong>Flood</strong>, <strong>Tornado</strong> and <strong>Typhoon</strong> have caused the Greatest Damage to Properties.<br /><strong>Drought</strong> and <strong>Flood</strong> had been the causes for the Greatest Damage to Crops.</p>

<div id="conclusion" class="section level2">
<h2>Conclusion</h2>
<p>From these data, we found that <strong>Excessive Heat</strong> and <strong>Tornado</strong> are most harmful with respect to Population Health, while <strong>Flood</strong>, <strong>Drought</strong> and <strong>Hurricane/Typhoon</strong> have the greatest Economic Consequences.</p>
